Roosevelt avoided the State Department and conducted high-level diplomacy through his aides, especially Harry Hopkins, whose influence was bolstered by his control of the Lend-Lease funds.<sup id="cite_ref-289"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_note-289">[278]</a></sup>

#### Nuclear program

In August 1939, [Leo Szilard](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leo_Szilard "Leo Szilard") and [Albert Einstein](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein "Albert Einstein") sent the [Einstein–Szilárd letter](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Einstein%E2%80%93Szil%C3%A1rd_letter "Einstein–Szilárd letter") to Roosevelt, warning of the possibility of a German [project](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/German_nuclear_weapon_project "German nuclear weapon project") to develop [nuclear weapons](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nuclear_weapon "Nuclear weapon"). Szilard realized that the recently discovered process of [nuclear fission](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nuclear_fission "Nuclear fission") could be used to create a [weapon of mass destruction](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Weapon_of_mass_destruction "Weapon of mass destruction").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBrands2009678–80_290-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBrands2009678%E2%80%9380-290">[279]</a></sup> Roosevelt feared the consequences of allowing Germany to have sole possession of the technology and authorized preliminary research into nuclear weapons.<sup id="cite_ref-292"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_note-292">[l]</a></sup> After Pearl Harbor, the Roosevelt administration secured funding to continue research and selected General [Leslie Groves](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leslie_Groves "Leslie Groves") to oversee the [Manhattan Project](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Manhattan_Project "Manhattan Project"), which was charged with developing the first nuclear weapons. Roosevelt and Churchill agreed to jointly pursue the project, and Roosevelt helped ensure that American scientists cooperated with their British counterparts.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith2007578–81_293-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith2007578%E2%80%9381-293">[281]</a></sup>

#### Wartime conferences

Churchill, Roosevelt, and Stalin at the [Yalta Conference](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yalta_Conference "Yalta Conference"), February 1945, two months before Roosevelt's death

Roosevelt coined the term "[Four Policemen](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Four_Policemen "Four Policemen")" to refer to the "Big Four" Allied powers of World War II: the United States, the United Kingdom, the Soviet Union, and China. The "[Big Three](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Grand_Alliance_(World_War_II) "Grand Alliance (World War II)")" of Roosevelt, [Winston Churchill](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Winston_Churchill "Winston Churchill"), and Soviet leader [Joseph Stalin](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joseph_Stalin "Joseph Stalin"), together with Chinese Generalissimo [Chiang Kai-shek](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chiang_Kai-shek "Chiang Kai-shek"), cooperated informally on a plan in which American and British troops concentrated in the West; Soviet troops fought on the [Eastern front](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eastern_Front_(World_War_II) "Eastern Front (World War II)"); and Chinese, British and American troops fought in Asia and the Pacific. The United States also continued to send aid via the Lend-Lease program to the Soviet Union and other countries. The Allies formulated strategy in a series of high-profile conferences as well as by contact through diplomatic and military channels.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDoeneckeStoler2005109–10_294-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDoeneckeStoler2005109%E2%80%9310-294">[282]</a></sup> Beginning in May 1942, the Soviets urged an Anglo-American invasion of German-occupied France to divert troops from the Eastern front.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith2007557–59_295-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith2007557%E2%80%9359-295">[283]</a></sup> Concerned that their forces were not yet ready, Churchill and Roosevelt decided to delay such an invasion until at least 1943 and instead focus on a landing in North Africa, known as [Operation Torch](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Operation_Torch "Operation Torch").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith2007560–61_296-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith2007560%E2%80%9361-296">[284]</a></sup>

In November 1943, Roosevelt, Churchill, and Stalin met to discuss strategy and post-war plans at the [Tehran Conference](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tehran_Conference "Tehran Conference"), where Roosevelt met Stalin for the first time.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith2007587–88_297-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith2007587%E2%80%9388-297">[285]</a></sup> Britain and the United States committed to opening a second front against Germany in 1944, while Stalin committed to entering the war against Japan at an unspecified date. Subsequent conferences at [Bretton Woods](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bretton_Woods_Conference "Bretton Woods Conference") and [Dumbarton Oaks](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dumbarton_Oaks_Conference "Dumbarton Oaks Conference") established the framework for the post-war [international monetary system](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_monetary_systems "International monetary systems") and the [United Nations](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Nations "United Nations"), an intergovernmental organization similar to the failed League of Nations.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELeuchtenburg2015214–16_298-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_note-FOOTNOTELeuchtenburg2015214%E2%80%9316-298">[286]</a></sup> Taking up the [Wilsonian](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wilsonian "Wilsonian") mantle, Roosevelt pushed the establishment of the United Nations as his highest postwar priority. Roosevelt expected it would be controlled by Washington, Moscow, London and Beijing, and would resolve all major world problems.<sup id="cite_ref-299"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_note-299">[287]</a></sup>

Roosevelt, Churchill, and Stalin met for a second time at the February 1945 [Yalta Conference](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yalta_Conference "Yalta Conference") in Crimea. With the end of the war in Europe approaching, Roosevelt's primary focus was convincing Stalin to enter the war against Japan; the Joint Chiefs had estimated that an [American invasion of Japan](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Operation_Downfall "Operation Downfall") would cause as many as one million American casualties. In return, the Soviet Union was promised control of Asian territories such as [Sakhalin Island](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sakhalin_Island "Sakhalin Island"). The three leaders agreed to hold a conference in 1945 to establish the United Nations, and they also agreed on the structure of the [United Nations Security Council](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council "United Nations Security Council"), which would be charged with ensuring [international security](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_security "International security"). Roosevelt did not push for the immediate evacuation of Soviet soldiers from Poland, but he won the issuance of the Declaration on Liberated Europe, which promised free elections in countries that had been occupied by Germany. Germany itself would not be dismembered but would be jointly occupied by the United States, France, Britain, and the Soviet Union.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith2007623–24_300-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith2007623%E2%80%9324-300">[288]</a></sup> Against Soviet pressure, Roosevelt and Churchill refused to consent to impose huge reparations and deindustrialization on Germany after the war.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELeuchtenburg2015233–34_301-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_note-FOOTNOTELeuchtenburg2015233%E2%80%9334-301">[289]</a></sup> Roosevelt's role in the [Yalta Conference](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yalta_Conference "Yalta Conference") has been controversial; critics charge that he naively trusted the Soviet Union to allow free elections in Eastern Europe, while supporters argue that there was little more that Roosevelt could have done for the Eastern European countries given the Soviet occupation and the need for cooperation with the Soviet Union.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHerring2008584–87_302-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHerring2008584%E2%80%9387-302">[290]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ebumiller1_303-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_note-ebumiller1-303">[291]</a></sup>

#### Course of the war

The Allies invaded [French North Africa](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/French_North_Africa "French North Africa") in November 1942, securing the surrender of [Vichy French](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vichy_France "Vichy France") forces within days of landing.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith2007563–64_304-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith2007563%E2%80%9364-304">[292]</a></sup> At the January 1943 [Casablanca Conference](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Casablanca_Conference "Casablanca Conference"), the Allies agreed to defeat Axis forces in North Africa and then launch an invasion of Sicily, with an attack on France to take place in 1944. At the conference, Roosevelt also announced that he would only accept the [unconditional surrender](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Unconditional_surrender "Unconditional surrender") of Germany, Japan, and Italy.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith2007565–67_305-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith2007565%E2%80%9367-305">[293]</a></sup> In February 1943, the Soviet Union won a major victory at the [Battle of Stalingrad](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Stalingrad "Battle of Stalingrad"), and in May 1943, the Allies secured the surrender of over 250,000 German and Italian soldiers in North Africa, ending the [North African Campaign](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/North_African_Campaign "North African Campaign").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith2007573–74_306-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith2007573%E2%80%9374-306">[294]</a></sup> The Allies launched an [invasion of Sicily](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Allied_invasion_of_Sicily "Allied invasion of Sicily") in July 1943, capturing the island the following month.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith2007575–76_307-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith2007575%E2%80%9376-307">[295]</a></sup> In September 1943, the Allies secured an [armistice](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Armistice_of_Cassibile "Armistice of Cassibile") from Italian Prime Minister [Pietro Badoglio](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pietro_Badoglio "Pietro Badoglio"), but Germany quickly restored Mussolini to power.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith2007575–76_307-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith2007575%E2%80%9376-307">[295]</a></sup> The [Allied invasion of mainland Italy](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Allied_invasion_of_Italy "Allied invasion of Italy") commenced in September 1943, but the [Italian Campaign](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Italian_Campaign_(World_War_II) "Italian Campaign (World War II)") continued until 1945 as German and Italian troops resisted the Allied advance.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith2007581–82_308-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith2007581%E2%80%9382-308">[296]</a></sup>

 [](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Ww2_allied_axis_1944_dec.png)

The Allies (blue and red) and the Axis Powers (black) in December 1944

To command the invasion of France, Roosevelt chose General [Dwight D. Eisenhower](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dwight_D._Eisenhower "Dwight D. Eisenhower"), who had successfully commanded a multinational coalition in North Africa and Sicily.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith2007596–97_309-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith2007596%E2%80%9397-309">[297]</a></sup> Eisenhower launched [Operation Overlord](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Operation_Overlord "Operation Overlord") on June 6, 1944. Supported by 12,000 aircraft and the largest naval force ever assembled, the Allies successfully established a beachhead in [Normandy](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Normandy "Normandy") and then advanced further into France.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith2007598–99_288-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith2007598%E2%80%9399-288">[277]</a></sup> Though reluctant to back an unelected government, Roosevelt recognized [Charles de Gaulle](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Charles_de_Gaulle "Charles de Gaulle")'s [Provisional Government of the French Republic](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Provisional_Government_of_the_French_Republic "Provisional Government of the French Republic") as the de facto government of France in July 1944. After most of France had been liberated, Roosevelt granted formal recognition to de Gaulle's government in October 1944.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith2007613–17_310-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith2007613%E2%80%9317-310">[298]</a></sup> Over the following months, the Allies liberated more territory and [began the invasion of Germany](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Western_Allied_invasion_of_Germany "Western Allied invasion of Germany"). By April 1945, Nazi resistance was crumbling in the face of advances by both the Western Allies and the Soviet Union.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith2007630–31_311-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith2007630%E2%80%9331-311">[299]</a></sup>

In the opening weeks of the war, Japan conquered the Philippines and the British and Dutch colonies in Southeast Asia. The Japanese advance reached its maximum extent by June 1942, when the U.S. Navy scored a decisive victory at the [Battle of Midway](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Midway "Battle of Midway"). American and Australian forces then began a slow and costly strategy called [island hopping](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leapfrogging_(strategy) "Leapfrogging (strategy)") or [leapfrogging](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leapfrogging "Leapfrogging") through the Pacific Islands, with the objective of gaining bases from which strategic airpower could be brought to bear on Japan and from which Japan could ultimately be invaded. In contrast to Hitler, Roosevelt took no direct part in the tactical naval operations, though he approved strategic decisions.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBurns1970228_312-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBurns1970228-312">[300]</a></sup> Roosevelt gave way in part to insistent demands from the public and Congress that more effort be devoted against Japan, but he always insisted on Germany first. The strength of the Japanese navy was decimated in the [Battle of Leyte Gulf](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Leyte_Gulf "Battle of Leyte Gulf"), and by April 1945 the Allies had re-captured much of their lost territory in the Pacific.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBrands2009785_313-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBrands2009785-313">[301]</a></sup>

#### Home front

The home front was subject to dynamic social changes throughout the war, though domestic issues were no longer Roosevelt's most urgent policy concern. The military buildup spurred economic growth. Unemployment fell from 7.7 million in spring 1940 to 3.4 million in fall 1941 and to 1.5 million in fall 1942, out of a labor force of 54 million.<sup id="cite_ref-315"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_note-315">[m]</a></sup> There was a growing labor shortage, accelerating the second wave of the [Great Migration](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Great_Migration_(African_American) "Great Migration (African American)") of African Americans, farmers and rural populations to manufacturing centers. African Americans from the South went to California and other West Coast states for new jobs in the defense industry. To pay for increased government spending, in 1941 Roosevelt proposed that Congress enact an income tax rate of 99.5% on all income over $100,000; when the proposal failed, he issued an executive order imposing an income tax of 100% on income over $25,000, which Congress rescinded.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESchweikartAllen2004602_316-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_note-FOOTNOTESchweikartAllen2004602-316">[303]</a></sup> The [Revenue Act of 1942](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Revenue_Act_of_1942 "Revenue Act of 1942") instituted top tax rates as high as 94% (after accounting for the [excess profits tax](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Excess_profits_tax "Excess profits tax")), greatly increased the tax base, and instituted the first federal [withholding tax](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Withholding_tax "Withholding tax").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELeuchtenburg2015221–22_317-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_note-FOOTNOTELeuchtenburg2015221%E2%80%9322-317">[304]</a></sup> In 1944, Roosevelt requested that Congress enact legislation to tax all "unreasonable" profits, both corporate and individual, and thereby support his declared need for over $10 billion in revenue for the war and other government measures. Congress overrode Roosevelt's veto to pass a [smaller revenue bill](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Individual_Income_Tax_Act_of_1944 "Individual Income Tax Act of 1944") raising $2 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBurns1970436_318-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBurns1970436-318">[305]</a></sup>

In 1942, war production increased dramatically but fell short of Roosevelt's goals, due in part to manpower shortages.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBurns1970333_319-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBurns1970333-319">[306]</a></sup> The effort was also hindered by numerous strikes, especially in the coal mining and railroad industries, which lasted well into 1944.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBurns1970343_320-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBurns1970343-320">[307]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHerman2012139–44,_151,_246_321-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHerman2012139%E2%80%9344,_151,_246-321">[308]</a></sup> Nonetheless, between 1941 and 1945, the United States produced 2.4 million trucks, 300,000 military aircraft, 88,400 tanks, and 40 billion rounds of ammunition. The production capacity of the United States dwarfed that of other countries; for example, in 1944, the United States produced more military aircraft than the combined production of Germany, Japan, Britain, and the Soviet Union.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith2007571–72_322-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith2007571%E2%80%9372-322">[309]</a></sup> The White House became the ultimate site for labor mediation, conciliation or arbitration. One particular battle royale occurred between Vice President Wallace, who headed the [Board of Economic Warfare](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Board_of_Economic_Warfare "Board of Economic Warfare"), and [Jesse H. Jones](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jesse_H._Jones "Jesse H. Jones"), in charge of the [Reconstruction Finance Corporation](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reconstruction_Finance_Corporation "Reconstruction Finance Corporation"); both agencies assumed responsibility for the acquisition of rubber supplies and came to loggerheads over funding. Roosevelt resolved the dispute by dissolving both agencies.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBurns1970339–42_323-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBurns1970339%E2%80%9342-323">[310]</a></sup> In 1943, Roosevelt established the [Office of War Mobilization](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Office_of_War_Mobilization "Office of War Mobilization") to oversee the home front; the agency was led by [James F. Byrnes](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/James_F._Byrnes "James F. Byrnes"), who came to be known as the "assistant president" due to his influence.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith2007575–76_307-2"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith2007575%E2%80%9376-307">[295]</a></sup>

[](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Second_Bill_of_Rights_Speech.ogv "Play video")Duration: 1 minute and 35 seconds.Subtitles available.[](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Second_Bill_of_Rights_Speech.ogv)

Roosevelt announced the plan for a [bill of social and economic rights](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Second_Bill_of_Rights "Second Bill of Rights") in the [State of the Union address](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/State_of_the_Union_address "State of the Union address") broadcast on January 11, 1944 (excerpt).

Roosevelt's 1944 [State of the Union Address](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/State_of_the_Union_Address "State of the Union Address") advocated that Americans should think of basic economic rights as a [Second Bill of Rights](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Second_Bill_of_Rights "Second Bill of Rights").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELeuchtenburg2015223–25_324-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_note-FOOTNOTELeuchtenburg2015223%E2%80%9325-324">[311]</a></sup> He stated that all Americans should have the right to "adequate medical care", "a good education", "a decent home", and a "useful and remunerative job".<sup id="cite_ref-zeitzsbr_325-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_note-zeitzsbr-325">[312]</a></sup> In the most ambitious domestic proposal of his third term, Roosevelt proposed the [G.I. Bill](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/G.I._Bill "G.I. Bill"), which would create a massive benefits program for returning soldiers. Benefits included [post-secondary education](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Higher_education "Higher education"), medical care, unemployment insurance, job counseling, and low-cost loans for homes and businesses. The G.I. Bill passed unanimously in both houses of Congress and was signed into law in June 1944. Of the fifteen million Americans who served in World War II, more than half benefitted from the educational opportunities provided for in the G.I. Bill.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith2007584–85_326-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith2007584%E2%80%9385-326">[313]</a></sup>

#### Declining health

Roosevelt, a [chain-smoker](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chain_smoking "Chain smoking") throughout his adult life,<sup id="cite_ref-nih_327-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_note-nih-327">[314]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-smoker_328-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_note-smoker-328">[315]</a></sup> had been in declining health since at least 1940. In March 1944, shortly after his 62nd birthday, he underwent testing at [Bethesda Hospital](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bethesda_Naval_Hospital "Bethesda Naval Hospital") and was found to have [hypertension](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hypertension "Hypertension"), [atherosclerosis](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atherosclerosis "Atherosclerosis"), [coronary artery disease](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Coronary_artery_disease "Coronary artery disease") causing [angina pectoris](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Angina_pectoris "Angina pectoris"), and [congestive heart failure](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Congestive_heart_failure "Congestive heart failure").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBurns1970448_329-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBurns1970448-329">[316]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-330"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_note-330">[317]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-331"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_note-331">[318]</a></sup>

Hospital physicians and two outside specialists ordered Roosevelt to rest. His personal physician, Admiral Ross McIntire, created a daily schedule that banned business guests for lunch and incorporated two hours of rest daily. During the 1944 re-election campaign, McIntire denied several times that Roosevelt's health was poor; on October 12, for example, he announced that "The President's health is perfectly OK. There are absolutely no organic difficulties at all."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGunther1950372–74_332-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGunther1950372%E2%80%9374-332">[319]</a></sup> Roosevelt realized that his declining health could eventually make it impossible for him to continue as president, and in 1945 he told a confidant that he might resign from the presidency following the end of the war.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDallek2017618–19_333-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDallek2017618%E2%80%9319-333">[320]</a></sup>

#### Election of 1944

 [](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:ElectoralCollege1944.svg)

1944 electoral vote results

While some Democrats had opposed Roosevelt's nomination in 1940, the president faced little difficulty in securing his re-nomination at the [1944 Democratic National Convention](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/1944_Democratic_National_Convention "1944 Democratic National Convention"). Roosevelt made it clear before the convention that he was seeking another term, and on the lone presidential ballot of the convention, Roosevelt won the vast majority of delegates, although a minority of Southern Democrats voted for [Harry F. Byrd](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_F._Byrd "Harry F. Byrd"). Party leaders prevailed upon Roosevelt to drop Vice President Wallace from the ticket, believing him to be an electoral liability and a poor potential successor in case of Roosevelt's death. Roosevelt preferred Byrnes as Wallace's replacement but was convinced to support Senator [Harry S. Truman](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_S._Truman "Harry S. Truman") of Missouri, who had earned renown for his investigation of [war production inefficiency](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Truman_Committee "Truman Committee") and was acceptable to the various factions of the party. On the second vice presidential ballot of the convention, Truman defeated Wallace to win the nomination.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith2007617–19_334-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith2007617%E2%80%9319-334">[321]</a></sup>

The Republicans nominated [Thomas E. Dewey](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thomas_E._Dewey "Thomas E. Dewey"), the governor of New York, who had a reputation as a liberal in his party. They accused the Roosevelt administration of domestic corruption and bureaucratic inefficiency, but Dewey's most effective gambit was to raise discreetly the age issue. He assailed the President as a "tired old man" with "tired old men" in his cabinet, pointedly suggesting that the President's lack of vigor had produced a less than vigorous economic recovery.<sup id="cite_ref-FDR_Campaigns_136-10"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_note-FDR_Campaigns-136">[133]</a></sup> Roosevelt, as most observers could see from his weight loss and haggard appearance, was a tired man in 1944. But upon entering the campaign in earnest in late September 1944, Roosevelt displayed enough passion to allay most concerns and deflect Republican attacks. With the war still raging, he urged voters not to "change horses in mid-stream."<sup id="cite_ref-FDR_Campaigns_136-11"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_note-FDR_Campaigns-136">[133]</a></sup> Labor unions, which had grown rapidly in the war, fully supported Roosevelt. Roosevelt and Truman won the [1944 election](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/1944_United_States_presidential_election "1944 United States presidential election"), defeating Dewey and his running mate [John W. Bricker](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_W._Bricker "John W. Bricker") with 53.4% of the popular vote and 432 out of the 531 electoral votes.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJordan2011321_335-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJordan2011321-335">[322]</a></sup> The president campaigned in favor of a strong United Nations, so his victory symbolized support for the nation's future participation in the international community.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBurns1970533,_562_336-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBurns1970533,_562-336">[323]</a></sup>

#### Final months and death

Last photograph of Roosevelt, taken April 11, 1945, the day before his death

Roosevelt's funeral procession in Washington, D.C., watched by 300,000 spectators, April 14, 1945

When Roosevelt returned to the United States from the [Yalta Conference](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yalta_Conference "Yalta Conference"), many were shocked to see how old, thin and frail he looked. He spoke while seated in the well of the House, an unprecedented concession to his physical incapacity.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDallek1995520_337-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDallek1995520-337">[324]</a></sup> During March 1945, he sent strongly worded messages to Stalin accusing him of breaking his Yalta commitments over Poland, Germany, [prisoners of war](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prisoner_of_war "Prisoner of war") and other issues. When Stalin accused the western Allies of plotting behind his back a separate peace with Hitler, Roosevelt replied: "I cannot avoid a feeling of bitter resentment towards your informers, whoever they are, for such vile misrepresentations of my actions or those of my trusted subordinates."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBurns1970587_338-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBurns1970587-338">[325]</a></sup> On March 29, 1945, Roosevelt went to the [Little White House](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Little_White_House "Little White House") at Warm Springs, Georgia, to rest before his anticipated appearance at the [founding conference](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Nations_Conference_on_International_Organization "United Nations Conference on International Organization") of the [United Nations](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Nations "United Nations").<sup>[<i><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2023)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>

In the afternoon of April 12, 1945, in [Warm Springs, Georgia](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Warm_Springs,_Georgia "Warm Springs, Georgia"), while sitting for [a portrait](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Unfinished_portrait_of_Franklin_D._Roosevelt "Unfinished portrait of Franklin D. Roosevelt") by [Elizabeth Shoumatoff](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Elizabeth_Shoumatoff "Elizabeth Shoumatoff"), Roosevelt said: "I have a terrific headache."<sup id="cite_ref-dayb_339-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_note-dayb-339">[326]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-340"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_note-340">[327]</a></sup> He then slumped forward in his chair, unconscious, and was carried into his bedroom. The president's attending cardiologist, [Howard Bruenn](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Howard_Bruenn "Howard Bruenn"), diagnosed a massive [intracerebral hemorrhage](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Intracerebral_hemorrhage "Intracerebral hemorrhage").<sup id="cite_ref-341"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_note-341">[328]</a></sup> At 3:35 p.m., Roosevelt died at the age of 63.<sup id="cite_ref-342"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_note-342">[329]</a></sup>

The following morning, Roosevelt's body was placed in a flag-draped coffin and loaded onto the presidential train for the trip back to Washington.<sup id="cite_ref-343"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_note-343">[330]</a></sup> Thousands flocked to the route to pay their respects. After a White House funeral on April 14, Roosevelt was transported by train from Washington to his birthplace at Hyde Park. On April 15 he was buried, per his wish, in the rose garden of his [Springwood estate](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Home_of_Franklin_D._Roosevelt_National_Historic_Site "Home of Franklin D. Roosevelt National Historic Site").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDallek2017620_344-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDallek2017620-344">[331]</a></sup>

Roosevelt's declining physical health had been kept secret from the public. His death was met with shock and grief across the world.<sup id="cite_ref-345"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_note-345">[332]</a></sup> Germany surrendered during the 30-day mourning period, but Harry Truman (who had succeeded Roosevelt as president) ordered flags to remain at half-staff; he also dedicated [Victory in Europe Day](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Victory_in_Europe_Day "Victory in Europe Day") and its celebrations to Roosevelt's memory.<sup id="cite_ref-346"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_note-346">[333]</a></sup> World War II ended with the signed [surrender of Japan](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Surrender_of_Japan "Surrender of Japan") in September.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELeuchtenburg2015243–52_347-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_note-FOOTNOTELeuchtenburg2015243%E2%80%9352-347">[334]</a></sup>

## Civil rights, repatriation, internment, and the Jews

 [](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Froosevelt.jpeg)

Official portrait of President Roosevelt by [Frank O. Salisbury](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Frank_O._Salisbury "Frank O. Salisbury"), c. 1947

Roosevelt was viewed as a hero by many African Americans, Catholics, and Jews, and he was highly successful in attracting large majorities of these voters into his New Deal coalition.<sup id="cite_ref-348"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_note-348">[335]</a></sup> From his first term until 1939, the [Mexican Repatriation](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mexican_Repatriation "Mexican Repatriation") started by President [Herbert Hoover](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Herbert_Hoover "Herbert Hoover") continued under Roosevelt, which scholars today contend was a form of [ethnic cleansing](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ethnic_cleansing "Ethnic cleansing") towards [Mexican Americans](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mexican_Americans "Mexican Americans"). Roosevelt ended federal involvement in the deportations. After 1934, deportations fell by approximately 50 percent.<sup id="cite_ref-Balderrama_349-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_note-Balderrama-349">[336]</a></sup> However, Roosevelt did not attempt to suppress the deportations on a local or state level.<sup id="cite_ref-350"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_note-350">[337]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-351"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_note-351">[338]</a></sup> Mexican Americans were the only group explicitly excluded from New Deal benefits. The deprival of [due process](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Due_process "Due process") for Mexican Americans is cited as a precedent for Roosevelt's [internment of Japanese Americans](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Internment_of_Japanese_Americans "Internment of Japanese Americans") in [concentration camps](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Concentration_camp "Concentration camp") during World War II.<sup id="cite_ref-EthnicCleansingJohnson_352-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_note-EthnicCleansingJohnson-352">[339]</a></sup> Roosevelt won strong support from Chinese Americans and Filipino Americans, but not Japanese Americans, as he presided over their internment during the war.<sup id="cite_ref-353"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_note-353">[340]</a></sup> African Americans and [Native Americans](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Native_Americans_in_the_United_States "Native Americans in the United States") fared well in two New Deal relief programs, the [Civilian Conservation Corps](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Civilian_Conservation_Corps "Civilian Conservation Corps") and the [Indian Reorganization Act](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indian_Reorganization_Act "Indian Reorganization Act"), respectively. Sitkoff reports that the WPA "provided an economic floor for the whole black community in the 1930s, rivaling both agriculture and domestic service as the chief source" of income.<sup id="cite_ref-354"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_note-354">[341]</a></sup>

### Lynching and civil rights

In contrast to Presidents Harding and Coolidge, Roosevelt stopped short of joining [NAACP](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/NAACP "NAACP") leaders in pushing for federal anti-[lynching](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lynching "Lynching") legislation. He asserted that such legislation was unlikely to pass and that his support for it would alienate Southern congressmen, though by 1940 even his conservative Texas vice-president, Garner, supported federal action against lynching.<sup id="cite_ref-355"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_note-355">[342]</a></sup>

Roosevelt did not appoint or nominate a single African American as secretary or assistant secretary to his cabinet. About one hundred African Americans met informally, however, to provide the administration with advice on issues related to African Americans. Although sometimes described as a "[Black Cabinet](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Black_Cabinet "Black Cabinet")", Roosevelt never officially acknowledged it as such nor did he make "appointments" to it.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcJimsey2000162–63_356-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcJimsey2000162%E2%80%9363-356">[343]</a></sup>

First Lady Eleanor Roosevelt vocally supported efforts designed to aid the African American community, including the Fair Labor Standards Act, which helped boost wages for nonwhite workers in the South.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDallek2017307–08_357-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDallek2017307%E2%80%9308-357">[344]</a></sup> In 1941, Roosevelt established the [Fair Employment Practices Committee](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fair_Employment_Practices_Committee "Fair Employment Practices Committee") (FEPC) to implement [Executive Order 8802](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Executive_Order_8802 "Executive Order 8802"), which prohibited racial and religious discrimination in employment among defense contractors. The FEPC was the first national program directed against [employment discrimination](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Employment_discrimination "Employment discrimination"), and it played a major role in opening up new employment opportunities to nonwhite workers. During World War II, the proportion of African American men employed in manufacturing positions rose significantly.<sup id="cite_ref-collins_358-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_note-collins-358">[345]</a></sup> In response to Roosevelt's policies, African Americans increasingly defected from the Republican Party during the 1930s and 1940s, becoming an important Democratic [voting bloc](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Voting_bloc "Voting bloc") in several Northern states.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcJimsey2000162–63_356-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcJimsey2000162%E2%80%9363-356">[343]</a></sup>

### Japanese Americans

The attack on Pearl Harbor raised concerns among the public regarding the possibility of sabotage by [Japanese Americans](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Japanese_Americans "Japanese Americans"). This suspicion was fed by long-standing racism against Japanese immigrants, as well as the findings of the [Roberts Commission](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roberts_Commissions "Roberts Commissions"), which concluded that the attack on Pearl Harbor had been assisted by Japanese spies. On February 19, 1942, Roosevelt signed [Executive Order 9066](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Executive_Order_9066 "Executive Order 9066"), which relocated 110,000 Japanese-American citizens and immigrants, most of whom lived on the Pacific Coast.<sup id="cite_ref-FDR_Domestic_Affairs_157-9"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_note-FDR_Domestic_Affairs-157">[153]</a></sup> They were forced to liquidate their properties and businesses and [interned in hastily built camps](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Internment_of_Japanese_Americans "Internment of Japanese Americans") in interior, harsh locations.

Roosevelt delegated the decision for internment to Secretary of War Stimson, who in turn relied on the judgment of Assistant Secretary of War [John J. McCloy](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_J._McCloy "John J. McCloy"). The Supreme Court upheld the constitutionality of the executive order in the 1944 case of _[Korematsu v. United States](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Korematsu_v._United_States "Korematsu v. United States")_.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith2007549–53_359-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith2007549%E2%80%9353-359">[346]</a></sup> A much smaller number of [German](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Internment_of_German_Americans "Internment of German Americans") and [Italian](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Internment_of_Italian_Americans "Internment of Italian Americans") citizens were arrested or placed into internment camps. Unlike Japanese Americans, however, they were not sent to them on the sole basis of racial ancestry.<sup id="cite_ref-360"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_note-360">[347]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-361"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_note-361">[348]</a></sup>

### Jews

There is controversy among historians about Roosevelt's attitude to Jews and the Holocaust. [Arthur M. Schlesinger Jr.](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arthur_M._Schlesinger_Jr. "Arthur M. Schlesinger Jr.") says Roosevelt "did what he could do" to help Jews; [David Wyman](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/David_Wyman "David Wyman") says Roosevelt's record on Jewish refugees and their rescue is "very poor" and one of the worst failures of his presidency.<sup id="cite_ref-362"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_note-362">[349]</a></sup> In 1923, as a member of the [Harvard University](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harvard_University "Harvard University") board of directors, Roosevelt decided there were too many Jewish students at Harvard and helped institute a quota to limit the number of Jews admitted.<sup id="cite_ref-latimes.com_363-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_note-latimes.com-363">[350]</a></sup> After Kristallnacht in 1938, Roosevelt had his ambassador to Germany recalled to Washington. He did not loosen immigration quotas but did allow German Jews already in the U.S. on visas to stay indefinitely.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBreitmanLichtman2013114–15_364-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBreitmanLichtman2013114%E2%80%9315-364">[351]</a></sup> According to [Rafael Medoff](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rafael_Medoff "Rafael Medoff"), Roosevelt could have saved 190,000 Jewish lives by telling his State Department to fill immigration quotas to the legal limit, but his administration discouraged and disqualified Jewish refugees based on its prohibitive requirements that left less than 25% of the quotas filled.<sup id="cite_ref-latimes.com_363-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_note-latimes.com-363">[350]</a></sup>

Hitler chose to implement the "[Final Solution](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Final_Solution "Final Solution")"—the extermination of the European Jewish population—by January 1942, and American officials learned of the scale of the Nazi extermination campaign in the following months. Against the objections of the State Department, Roosevelt convinced the other Allied leaders to issue the [Joint Declaration by Members of the United Nations](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joint_Declaration_by_Members_of_the_United_Nations "Joint Declaration by Members of the United Nations"), which condemned the ongoing [Holocaust](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Holocaust "The Holocaust") and warned to try its perpetrators as [war criminals](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/War_crime "War crime"). In 1943, Roosevelt told U.S. government officials that there should be limits on Jews in various professions to "eliminate the specific and understandable complaints which the Germans bore towards the Jews in Germany."<sup id="cite_ref-latimes.com_363-2"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_note-latimes.com-363">[350]</a></sup> The same year, Roosevelt was personally briefed by [Polish Home Army](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polish_Home_Army "Polish Home Army") intelligence agent [Jan Karski](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jan_Karski "Jan Karski") who was an eyewitness of the Holocaust; pleading for action, Karski told him that 1.8 million Jews had already been exterminated.<sup id="cite_ref-365"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_note-365">[352]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-366"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_note-366">[353]</a></sup> Karski recalled that Roosevelt "did not ask one question about the Jews."<sup id="cite_ref-367"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_note-367">[354]</a></sup> In January 1944, Roosevelt established the [War Refugee Board](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/War_Refugee_Board "War Refugee Board") to aid Jews and other victims of Axis atrocities. Aside from these actions, Roosevelt believed that the best way to help the persecuted populations of Europe was to end the war as quickly as possible. Top military leaders and War Department leaders rejected any campaign to bomb the [extermination camps](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Extermination_camps "Extermination camps") or the rail lines leading to them, fearing it would be a diversion from the war effort. According to biographer [Jean Edward Smith](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jean_Edward_Smith "Jean Edward Smith"), there is no evidence that anyone ever proposed such a campaign to Roosevelt.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith2007607–13_368-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith2007607%E2%80%9313-368">[355]</a></sup>

## Legacy

### Historical reputation

Roosevelt is widely considered to be one of the most important figures in the [history of the United States](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_the_United_States "History of the United States"),<sup id="cite_ref-100mostinfluential_369-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_note-100mostinfluential-369">[356]</a></sup> as well as one of the most influential figures of the 20th century.<sup id="cite_ref-kwalsh1_370-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_note-kwalsh1-370">[357]</a></sup> Historians and political scientists consistently rank Roosevelt, [George Washington](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/George_Washington "George Washington"), and [Abraham Lincoln](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abraham_Lincoln "Abraham Lincoln") as the three [greatest presidents](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Historical_rankings_of_presidents_of_the_United_States "Historical rankings of presidents of the United States"), although the order varies.<sup id="cite_ref-greatestpresidents_371-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_note-greatestpresidents-371">[358]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-greatestpresidents2_372-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_note-greatestpresidents2-372">[359]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-greatestpresidents3_373-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_note-greatestpresidents3-373">[360]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-374"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_note-374">[361]</a></sup> Reflecting on Roosevelt's presidency, "which brought the United States through the Great Depression and World War II to a prosperous future", biographer [Jean Edward Smith](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jean_Edward_Smith "Jean Edward Smith") said in 2007, "He lifted himself from a wheelchair to lift the nation from its knees."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith2007ix_375-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith2007ix-375">[362]</a></sup>

His commitment to the working class and unemployed in need of relief in the nation's longest recession made him a favorite of blue-collar workers, labor unions, and ethnic minorities.<sup id="cite_ref-376"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_note-376">[363]</a></sup> The rapid expansion of government programs that occurred during Roosevelt's term redefined the role of government in the United States, and Roosevelt's advocacy for government social programs was instrumental in redefining [liberalism](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Modern_liberalism_in_the_United_States "Modern liberalism in the United States") for coming generations.<sup id="cite_ref-377"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_note-377">[364]</a></sup> Roosevelt firmly established U.S. leadership on the world stage with his role in shaping and financing World War II. His isolationist critics faded away, and even the Republicans joined in his overall policies.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlack20051126–27_378-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlack20051126%E2%80%9327-378">[365]</a></sup> He also permanently increased the power of the president at the expense of Congress.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELeuchtenburg2015174–75_379-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_note-FOOTNOTELeuchtenburg2015174%E2%80%9375-379">[366]</a></sup>

His Second Bill of Rights became, according to historian Joshua Zeitz, "the basis of the Democratic Party's aspirations for the better part of four decades."<sup id="cite_ref-zeitzsbr_325-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_note-zeitzsbr-325">[312]</a></sup> After his death, Eleanor continued to be a forceful presence in U.S. and world politics, serving as delegate to the conference which established the United Nations and championing civil rights and liberalism generally. Some junior New Dealers played leading roles in the presidencies of Truman, John Kennedy, and Lyndon Johnson. Kennedy came from a Roosevelt-hating family. Historian [William Leuchtenburg](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/William_Leuchtenburg "William Leuchtenburg") says that before 1960, "Kennedy showed a conspicuous lack of inclination to identify himself as a New Deal liberal." He adds, as president, "Kennedy never wholly embraced the Roosevelt tradition and at times he deliberately severed himself from it."<sup id="cite_ref-380"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_note-380">[367]</a></sup> By contrast, young Lyndon Johnson had been an enthusiastic New Dealer and a favorite of Roosevelt. Johnson modelled his presidency on Roosevelt's and relied heavily on New Deal lawyer [Abe Fortas](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abe_Fortas "Abe Fortas"), as well as [James H. Rowe](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/James_H._Rowe "James H. Rowe"), [Anna M. Rosenberg](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anna_M._Rosenberg "Anna M. Rosenberg"), [Thomas Gardiner Corcoran](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thomas_Gardiner_Corcoran "Thomas Gardiner Corcoran"), and [Benjamin V. Cohen](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Benjamin_V._Cohen "Benjamin V. Cohen").<sup id="cite_ref-381"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_note-381">[368]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-382"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_note-382">[369]</a></sup>

During his presidency, and continuing to a lesser extent afterwards, there has been much [criticism of Roosevelt](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Criticism_of_Franklin_D._Roosevelt "Criticism of Franklin D. Roosevelt"), some of it intense. Critics have questioned not only [his policies, positions](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Critics_of_the_New_Deal "Critics of the New Deal"), and the consolidation of power that occurred due to his responses to the Depression and World War II but also his breaking with tradition by running for a third term as president.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDallek2017624–25_383-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDallek2017624%E2%80%9325-383">[370]</a></sup> Long after his death, new lines of attack criticized Roosevelt's policies regarding helping the Jews of Europe,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWyman1984_384-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWyman1984-384">[371]</a></sup> incarcerating the Japanese on the [West Coast](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/West_Coast_of_the_United_States "West Coast of the United States"),<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobinson2001_385-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobinson2001-385">[372]</a></sup> and opposing anti-lynching legislation.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDallek2017626_386-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDallek2017626-386">[373]</a></sup>

Roosevelt was criticized by conservatives for his economic policies, especially the shift in tone from [individualism](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Individualism "Individualism") to [collectivism](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Collectivism_and_individualism "Collectivism and individualism") with the expansion of the [welfare state](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Welfare_state "Welfare state") and regulation of the economy. Those criticisms continued decades after his death. One factor in the revisiting of these issues was the election of [Ronald Reagan](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ronald_Reagan "Ronald Reagan") in 1980, who opposed the New Deal.<sup id="cite_ref-387"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_note-387">[374]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-388"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_note-388">[375]</a></sup>

### Memorials

Roosevelt's [home in Hyde Park](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Home_of_Franklin_D._Roosevelt_National_Historic_Site "Home of Franklin D. Roosevelt National Historic Site") is now a [National Historic Site](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Historic_Sites_(United_States) "National Historic Sites (United States)") and home to his [Presidential library](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt_Presidential_Library_and_Museum "Franklin D. Roosevelt Presidential Library and Museum"). Washington, D.C., hosts two memorials: the 7+1⁄2\-acre (3-hectare) [Roosevelt Memorial](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_Delano_Roosevelt_Memorial "Franklin Delano Roosevelt Memorial"), located next to the [Jefferson Memorial](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jefferson_Memorial "Jefferson Memorial") on the [Tidal Basin](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tidal_Basin "Tidal Basin"),<sup id="cite_ref-npsmem1_389-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_note-npsmem1-389">[376]</a></sup> and a [more modest memorial](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_Delano_Roosevelt_Memorial#Original_Franklin_Delano_Roosevelt_Memorial "Franklin Delano Roosevelt Memorial"), a block of marble in front of the National Archives building suggested by Roosevelt himself, erected in 1965.<sup id="cite_ref-390"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_note-390">[377]</a></sup> Roosevelt's leadership in the [March of Dimes](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/March_of_Dimes "March of Dimes") is one reason he is commemorated on the American [dime](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dime_(United_States_coin) "Dime (United States coin)").<sup id="cite_ref-dime1_391-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_note-dime1-391">[378]</a></sup> Roosevelt has also appeared on several [U.S. Postage stamps](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/U.S._Presidents_on_U.S._postage_stamps#Franklin_D._Roosevelt "U.S. Presidents on U.S. postage stamps").<sup id="cite_ref-392"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_note-392">[379]</a></sup> On April 29, 1945, seventeen days after Roosevelt's death, the carrier [USS _Franklin D. Roosevelt_](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/USS_Franklin_D._Roosevelt_(CV-42) "USS Franklin D. Roosevelt (CV-42)") was launched and served from 1945 to 1977.<sup id="cite_ref-393"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_note-393">[380]</a></sup> London's [Westminster Abbey](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Westminster_Abbey "Westminster Abbey") also has a stone tablet memorial to Roosevelt that was unveiled by [Attlee](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Clement_Attlee "Clement Attlee") and Churchill in 1948.<sup id="cite_ref-394"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_note-394">[381]</a></sup> [Welfare Island](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roosevelt_Island "Roosevelt Island") was renamed after Roosevelt in September 1973.<sup id="cite_ref-395"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_note-395">[382]</a></sup>

-   1948 statue of Roosevelt in [Grosvenor Square](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Grosvenor_Square "Grosvenor Square"), London
    
-   Engraving of the [Four Freedoms](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Four_Freedoms "Four Freedoms") at the [Franklin Delano Roosevelt Memorial](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_Delano_Roosevelt_Memorial "Franklin Delano Roosevelt Memorial"), dedicated in 1997 in Washington, D.C.

## Notes

1.  **[^](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_ref-2 "Jump up")** Pronounced [_DEL\-ə-noh ROH\-zə-velt, -⁠vəlt_](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Help:Pronunciation_respelling_key "Help:Pronunciation respelling key");<sup id="cite_ref-AHD_1-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_note-AHD-1">[1]</a></sup>
2.  **[^](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_ref-29 "Jump up")** In 2008, Columbia awarded Roosevelt a posthumous [Juris Doctor](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Juris_Doctor "Juris Doctor") degree.<sup id="cite_ref-posthumousjd_28-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_note-posthumousjd-28">[27]</a></sup>
3.  **[^](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_ref-57 "Jump up")** State legislatures elected United States senators prior to the ratification of the [Seventeenth Amendment](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Seventeenth_Amendment_to_the_United_States_Constitution "Seventeenth Amendment to the United States Constitution") in 1913.
4.  **[^](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_ref-147 "Jump up")** Roosevelt was the last president inaugurated on March 4. The [Twentieth Amendment](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Twentieth_Amendment_to_the_United_States_Constitution "Twentieth Amendment to the United States Constitution") changed presidential inaugurations to January 20, from 1937.
5.  **[^](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_ref-188 "Jump up")** Biographer [Jean Edward Smith](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jean_Edward_Smith "Jean Edward Smith") notes that "the significance of the repeal of the two-thirds rule...is difficult to overstate. Not only did the power of the South in the Democratic party diminish, but without the repeal, it is open to question whether FDR could have been renominated in 1940."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith2007366_187-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith2007366-187">[183]</a></sup>
6.  **[^](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_ref-190 "Jump up")** The [1964](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/1964_United_States_presidential_election "1964 United States presidential election") Democratic ticket of [Lyndon B. Johnson](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lyndon_B._Johnson "Lyndon B. Johnson") and [Hubert Humphrey](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hubert_Humphrey "Hubert Humphrey") would later set a new record, taking 61.1% of the popular vote
7.  **[^](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_ref-197 "Jump up")** The two Justices who Roosevelt did not originally appoint to the Court were [Harlan Fiske Stone](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harlan_Fiske_Stone "Harlan Fiske Stone") and [Owen Roberts](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Owen_Roberts "Owen Roberts"). However, in 1941, Roosevelt elevated Stone to the position of Chief Justice.
8.  **[^](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_ref-216 "Jump up")** This table shows the estimated unemployment related as calculated by two economists. Michael Darby's estimate counts individuals on work relief programs as employed, while Stanley Lebergott's estimate counts individuals on work relief programs as unemployed<sup id="cite_ref-margo1_215-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_note-margo1-215">[208]</a></sup>
9.  **[^](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_ref-243 "Jump up")** The [Twenty-second Amendment](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Twenty-second_Amendment_to_the_United_States_Constitution "Twenty-second Amendment to the United States Constitution") ratified in 1951, would bar any individual from winning more than two presidential elections.
10.  **[^](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_ref-273 "Jump up")** Hull and others in the administration were unwilling to recognize the Japanese conquest of China and feared that an American accommodation with Japan would leave the Soviet Union vulnerable to a two-front war.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith2007522–23_272-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith2007522%E2%80%9323-272">[263]</a></sup>
11.  **[^](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_ref-277 "Jump up")** The United States would also declare war on [Bulgaria](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kingdom_of_Bulgaria "Kingdom of Bulgaria"), [Hungary](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kingdom_of_Hungary_(1920%E2%80%9346) "Kingdom of Hungary (1920–46)"), and [Romania](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kingdom_of_Romania "Kingdom of Romania"), all of which had joined the Axis bloc.
12.  **[^](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_ref-292 "Jump up")** The Germans stopped research on nuclear weapons in 1942, choosing to focus on other projects. Japan gave up its own program in 1943.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith2007580_291-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith2007580-291">[280]</a></sup>
13.  **[^](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_ref-315 "Jump up")** WPA workers were counted as unemployed by this set of statistics.<sup id="cite_ref-314"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt#cite_note-314">[302]</a></sup>
